The Frontrunner


January 3, 2005 Monday


HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno: "Happy New Year, everybody. We are live tonight. Unfortunately, so is Bin Laden and Scott Peterson, but that's okay."

Jay Leno: "In just 25 minutes, Secretary Colin Powell will push the button to drop the ball in Times Square. Powell said the hardest part, getting a cab to take him." 

Jay Leno: "NBC gave me a Christmas gift that literally made my heart stop. It was a bottle of Aleve."

Jay Leno: "Drug companies are now asking their employees to be on the lookout for Michael Moore, who's making a movie about the pharmaceutical industry. Like 9/11, he's doing a movie about the drug industry. Do you have to be on the lookout for Michael Moore? Isn't he kind of easy to spot?"

Jay Leno: "Osama bin Laden has released yet another audiotape saying that any Iraqi voting in the January election will be considered an infidel and will be punished by God. And he also urged people not to waste their vote on Ralph Nader."

Jay Leno: "In Cuba, Fidel Castro says they have found a drilling site in Cuba with 100 million barrels of oil. How long before Bush says, 'People of Cuba, we are here to free you. You will no longer live under oppression and tyranny.'"

Conan O'Brien: "Here in New York, thousands of people partied in funny hats and popped balloons in Times Square. Yeah. Those who were there said it was just like the Republican Convention, but with black people."

Conan O'Brien: "President Bush said that he doesn't really celebrate New Year's Eve and plans on being in bed by 9:30. That's what he said. Meanwhile, Paris Hilton said she does celebrate New Year's Eve, and plans on being in bed by 9:30."

January 5, 2005 Wednesday


HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno:

"Fidel Castro has announced that an oil site with up to 100 million barrels of oil in it has been found off the coast of Cuba. The only problem is you give the Cubans 100 million barrels, the entire population will float to Miami in them." 

Jay Leno:

"Some good news -- the FBI now says today, there's no terrorist link involving people shining laser beams into the eyes of airline pilots. Turns out it was just pranksters. Whew, that makes me feel better."

Jay Leno:

"If you're on a flight, and your pilot suddenly goes, 'My eyes, my eyes!' Oh, it's just kids. Wacky pranksters."

Jay Leno:

"In the past three years, only 34 people have died in aviation accidents, making it one of the safest periods in history for the airlines. Isn't that amazing? You know what that means? The pilots were actually flying better when they were drunk."

Jay Leno:

Republican Christine Todd Whitman's new book "is called 'It's My Party, Too: The Battle for the Heart of the GOP.' See, that's the part I don't get. The battle for the heart of the Republican Party? Isn't that like fighting for the brain of the Democratic Party?"

Jay Leno:

"I don't know if anybody got this week's Newsweek, there's an interview in there with John Kerry. And John Kerry -- this is his quote -- John Kerry said he didn't lose the election, he just didn't win it. See, that's the kind of clear, decisive thinking we all loved about him."

Jay Leno:

"The Bush Administration's proposing a change to the Social Security system. They want to cut benefits by nearly a third in the next 20 years to 30 years. The new program is called 'Good luck, grandma. You're on your own. You've fallen and you can't get up!'"

David Letterman:

"Violent crime, according to the year-end statistics, violent crime in New York City is way, way down. It's amazing, isn't it? And it just goes to show you, you get Martha Stewart off the street and look what happens."

David Letterman:

"There's rumors that Osama bin Laden has moved to a major city. Isn't that odd? Apparently he plans to keep his cave for the weekends."

David Letterman:

"For the third year in a row, Oprah Winfrey was voted America's favorite TV personality. I'm very proud. I also was on that list. I was a little farther down. I was right between Bernard Kerik and Scott Peterson."

HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno:

"Congress returned to session yesterday after about a month off. Did you even notice that they were gone?"

Jay Leno:

"See, that's when you know you have a government job. Can you think of any other job where you leave for a month, and nobody even knows you weren't there?" 

Jay Leno:

"Congress has reelected Dennis Hastert as Speaker of the House. He's right after the vice president in line to the president. Which means he's a heartbeat away from a guy who barely has a heartbeat."

Jay Leno:

"Well, the good news, the government reports that there has been a big increase in factory orders. The bad news, most of the orders, to pack up the factory and move it to India."

David Letterman:

"I'm so happy we have a good group in the audience tonight, because last night the audience, whoa, horrible! ... Here's how lousy they were. After the show, they went out and pointed a laser beam at a jet."

David Letterman:

"Turned out it's a guy in New Jersey. You hear about this? He was pointing a high powered laser beam at jetliners as they would fly other his house. And they grabbed the guy and arrested the guy and everybody is okay. One good thing did come of the episode, the in-flight meals were warmed up a little from the laser, but that's..."

David Letterman:

"There was an animal rights group, I thought this was fascinating, they asked former President Carter to stop fishing. How about that? They told him to stop fishing, and I was thinking about this. This makes him the first president ever, I believe, told to put away his rod since since...well, Clinton."

Craig Ferguson:

"The new Cabinet in Washington, new ideas are coming out of there. A new one to eliminate the Social Security crisis and help with the war in Iraq. Draft the elderly."

HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno:

"It was so cold, pilots are asking people to shine lasers at them just for the warmth."

Jay Leno:

"Governor Schwarzenegger gave his state of the state address last night. He talked about his solution to the high cost of prescription drugs. He said, 'Stop whining, and walk it off. There is nothing wrong with a tumor you can't walk off.'" 

Jay Leno:

"President Bush has begun working on his inauguration day speech. He says that when he is sworn in, he will swear to preserve, protect, and defend the Constitution of the US and the treasure map that is drawn on the back."

Jay Leno:

"At the National Constitution Center in Philadelphia, tourists can experience what it is like to take the oath of office as president at a virtual swearing-in station. Your image is up on a giant screen while an actor playing a Supreme Court justice swears you in. Kind of like a fantasy camp for Democrats."

Jay Leno:

"Trent Lott, who is in charge of the inaugural ceremonies...he announced that one of the performers at the inaugural event this year is a former singer from the Lawrence Welk show who will sing a song by John Ashcroft. Who said the Republicans don't know how to party?"

Jay Leno:

"You know, if they did that at Guantanamo Bay, the Red Cross would declare it cruel and unusual punishment."

Jay Leno:

"Alberto Gonzales, nominee for US attorney general, answered some tough questions from Congress today about his role in the Iraqi prison torture scandal. But afterward, he said that to make himself relax, he said he used that old trick of imaging the audience in their underwear...with hoods over their heads, being lead around on a dog leash by a woman."

David Letterman:

"A guy in New Jersey was arrested because he was shooting laser beams at commercial jetliners. I'm telling you, it was so unnerving that the pilot poured himself another scotch."

Craig Ferguson:

"President Bush and his wife, they've got a new dog today. Isn't that cute? The little rascal has stained the rug in the Oval Office. So they had to name him Clinton."

Craig Ferguson:

"You know why the President had to get a new dog -- because the old one resigned."

HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno:

"Man, what a storm we had last night -- almost as many trees have been knocked down by this storm as been knocked down by the Bush Administration."

Jay Leno: 

"As you know, Michael Moore won a People's Choice award the other night. In fact, this may be the first time the Republicans asked for a recount."

Jay Leno:

"And today, President Bush admitted there are four areas of Iraq where it will be very difficult for people to vote. The east, the west, the north and the south."

Jay Leno:

"This is what President Bush said. He said, 'The election will go ahead as scheduled because it doesn't matter if nobody votes. The important thing here is to say you held an election.' Worked in Florida."

Jay Leno:

"President Bush -- getting ready for his inauguration next week, working on the speech. It's a pretty good speech. So far, we've got -- it's, 'Ask not what your corporation can do for you, but what you can do for your corporation.'"

Jay Leno:

"A big shake-up at CBS News over the story about President Bush and the falsified National Guard records. CBS issued a report saying 60 Minutes was misled by an unreliable source. Yeah, I think his name was Dan Rather, wasn't it?"

Jay Leno:

"Yesterday, when the report came out, Dan was not at his anchor spot at CBS. He didn't do it last night. They said he was on assignment. Oh, shut up. He was hiding in the basement."

Jay Leno:

"The independent counsel also" concluded "that CBS failed to follow basic journalistic principles in reporting. And then today, Fox said, 'So?'"

David Letterman:

"Thank you very much. I appreciate that, but honestly, how many of you folks are just here for the openings at CBS News?"

David Letterman:

"It's like a bloodbath over at CBS News. Have you heard about all of the firings? It's crazy. I believe the last time this many CBS executives got fired was, well, shortly after I was hired."

David Letterman:

"The people fired by CBS, you know, I heard about this. They were treated badly. The people who got fired by CBS News, and I'll got right on record and say it. They were treated shabbily. They were called together and forced to form a naked pyramid."

David Letterman:

"Did you hear about Mahmoud Abbas was elected president in Palestine? Did you hear about that? I understand the votes were counted by Mahmoud Abbas's brother, Jeb Abbas."

David Letterman:

"Guess who was at the Detroit auto show opening night? Bill Clinton, former President Bill Clinton, that's right, doing his part. And they have the beautiful auto show models, you know, demonstrating the cars like that, and he was seen talking to one of the auto show models, apparently about the price for a Hummer."

Craig Ferguson:

"They say that the security arrangements for the upcoming presidential inauguration will be the most extensive in history, and that's just to keep the Bush twins away from the champagne."

Craig Ferguson:

"CBS News today has fired four employees for wildly fabricating a news story. The good news, they all got jobs over at Fox."

HEADLINE: Late Night Political Humor


BODY:

Jay Leno:

"Do you realize there were more weapons found at Vitello's Restaurant than there were in Iraq. You know that?"

"This week, US authorities refused to allow a British Airways flight bound for New York to land on American soil, because a suspicious passenger was on board. They requested the flight be diverted to Bangor, Maine. Now, I'm no geography expert. How does that make the people of Bangor feel?" 

Jay Leno:

"What, did we lose Maine in a poker game? What happened?"

Jay Leno:

"The Commerce Department reported that the American trade deficit soared to an all-time high of $60 billion in November. That is unbelievable. It's so bad now, Mexicans are going to India to try and find good American jobs."

Jay Leno:

"In Virginia, President Bush announced tough new reading standards for high school students. He wants ninth graders to read at an eighth grade level by the time they're in the 12th grade."

Jay Leno:

"Major League Baseball announced their tougher steroid testing policies. The new steroid rules will impose a $100,000 fine for a five-time steroid offender. You know what the old penalty was for a five-time offender? Most valuable player trophy."

Jay Leno:

"You know what bothers me is the timing of all this steroid stuff. Maybe I'm paranoid because I'm from Boston, okay? After 86 years, the Boston Red Sox finally win the World Series. People are going, 'No, they got to be on something.'"

Jay Leno:

"The government issued new dietary guidelines today. ... You know, they come out with this food pyramid, what, every five years? You think that helps? Have you seen most Americans? We are food pyramids, okay?"

Jay Leno:

"How many watched the NBC show 'The Biggest Loser' the other night? One of the female finalists, Kelly Minor, she didn't win, but she lost 79 pounds. ... She looks great. She said she feels great. And finally, she stopped getting all those annoying calls from Bill Clinton."

David Letterman:

"President Bush now says that Saddam Hussein did not have weapons of mass destruction. Oh. I'll be darned."

David Letterman:

"Saddam Hussein did not have weapons of mass destruction, but Bush says there is strong evidence that Saddam Hussein had an illegal nanny."

Conan O'Brien:

"Today, the White House announced that Ruben Studdard will be performing at one of President Bush's inaugural celebrations. Republicans say they chose Studdard 'cause he's one of the red states."

Conan O'Brien:

"Major League Baseball announced today it's going to institute tougher steroid testing. For the first offense, players will receive a ten-game suspension, for the second offense, players will receive a batting championship."

Craig Ferguson:

"The White House officially concluded today that there are no weapons of mass destruction in Iraq. Boy, what a tough couple of months it's been for George Bush. This month, no weapons. Last month -- last month, no Santa."

Craig Ferguson:

"Major League Baseball has announced a tough new drug testing policy. Jason Giambi got confused by the new testing. He thought you were supposed to test every drug, so..."

Craig Ferguson:

"Doctors have pointed out one serious side effect of steroids. There is a slight chance you could become governor of California."

"This replaces the old policy of, 'Don't ask, don't tell.'"

Jay Leno:

"No, under the new agreement, players who test positive will now be slapped on both wrists."

"The new rules are a little bit tougher. They include random drug testing, suspension for a maximum of ten days for first-time offenders, and every time a player hits a home run, while rounding third base, they have to stop and pee in a little cup."

Jay Leno:

"And every single team in the league is subject to these testing guidelines. Well, except the Chicago Cubs -- they need all the help they can get."

"Officials in the State Department now say that in the Iraqi presidential elections, the Sunnis are refusing to vote. So you know what that means -- this whole thing is turning to Shiite now."

"The Army says that 28 prisoners escaped from the Abu Ghraib prison in Iraq. They're afraid the naked guys have blended in to a Christina Aguilera video. So we may never find them."
